[View Diff on GitHub](https://github.com/MicrosoftDocs/azure-ai-docs/compare/MicrosoftDocs:fd28ace...MicrosoftDocs:aedf0c1){target="_blank"}

```plaintext
# ハイライト
このアップデートは、さまざまなドキュメントのメタデータを更新し、特に日付関連の情報を最新のものに修正する軽微な変更です。新機能の追加や抜本的な変更は行われていませんが、ドキュメントの整合性を維持し、利用者に正確な情報を提供することを目的としています。

## 新機能
新機能として紹介されている要素はありません。

## 破壊的変更
破壊的な変更は含まれていません。

## その他の更新
- ドキュメントの日付を一斉に更新
- Java SDKやREST APIなどのクイックスタートガイドのフォーマットを整形
- カスタム質問応答や言語サポートに関するリタイア情報を簡潔化、より明確に
- および画像ファイルのメタデータ更新

# インサイト
このドキュメントセットの更新は、全体として利用者が常に最新の情報を保有できるよう支える重要な努力です。AIサービスやクラウド技術の領域では、情報が迅速に変わるため、このような定期的なメタデータの更新は欠かせません。特に、技術文書における日付の更新は、ユーザーが情報の新鮮さを確認し、信頼して依頼できることを保証します。

また、フォーマットの調整を行うことで、コードの可読性が向上し、開発者により明確な指示を提供できるようになります。これにより、特に視覚的な要素や同義語の統一により、情報の一貫性が確保され、学習や実装が円滑化されます。

さらに、リタイア情報の簡潔化により、利用者が将来のサービス変更に適切に対処できるようになっています。移行を促す具体的なアクション型のガイドは、混乱を避け、生産性を保持するために重要です。全体として、このマイナーな改訂は、利用者に質の高いユーザーエクスペリエンスを提供するための基礎を強化するものです。
```

## articles/ai-services/document-intelligence/reference/known-issues.md{#item-2c1011}

<details>
<summary>Diff</summary>
````diff
@@ -6,7 +6,7 @@ ai-usage: ai-assisted
 manager: mcleans
 ms.service: azure-document-intelligence-foundry-tools
 ms.topic: reference
-ms.date: 04/09/2026
+ms.date: 06/04/2026
 ms.author: lajanuar
 ---
 <!-- markdownlint-disable MD025 -->
@@ -27,11 +27,17 @@ The following table lists active, service-confirmed issues in Azure Document Int
 
 | Issue ID | Category | Title | Description | Workaround | Publication date |
 | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
-| **1001** | File types | `Content Is Not Supported Error With Excel Files` | Excel files are documented as a supported input type. Requests can fail with **Content isn't supported** when file content exceeds an internal character limit. This condition usually occurs with large or densely populated spreadsheets. | **Excel files larger than *~8,000,000 characters* are rejected**.<br><br>**Option A:** Split large Excel files into smaller files and submit them separately.<br><br>**Option B:** Switch to Azure [Content Understanding](../../content-understanding/overview.md), which uses improved parser logic for these files. | April  2026 |
- | **1002** | Encryption | `ServiceUnavailable error when using CMK` | Operations that rely on **Customer‑Managed Keys (CMK)** can intermittently fail with a **service unavailable** error. This failure occurs when the storage service uses stale cached identity or key material. | **Option A:** Refresh the `CMK` cache. Disable and re-enable `CMK`, assign a new key, or associate a new managed identity.<br><br>**Option B:** Switch to **Microsoft-Managed Keys (MMK)**: Navigate to your Document Intelligence resource in the [Azure portal](https://portal.azure.com/). **Resource Management** → **Encryption** -> **Microsoft Managed Keys**. | April  2026 |
-| **1003** | Model management | `Model Exists Error When Model Copy` | Copying a custom model can fail with a **Model Exists** error. This error occurs when a broken or partially created model remains on the target resource. Customers can't resolve this condition themselves. | No customer-side workaround is available.<br><br>Submit a [support request](mailto:formrecog_contact@microsoft.com) so the product group can remove the broken model from the backend. | April  2026 |
-| **1004** | Model training | `HTTP 500 – InternalServerError during model training (Neural or Template, Preview/GA APIs)` | Model training can fail with **HTTP 500 / InternalServerError**. This failure typically occurs when managed identity isn't configured correctly on the resource, especially in newer training flows. | Enable **Managed Identity** on your Document Intelligence resource.<br><br>Verify that the identity has the required permissions.<br><br>Follow the official [managed-identity configuration guidance](../authentication/managed-identities.md). | April  2026 |
-| **1005** | Model training | `Model training stuck in *Not started* status` | If a model training job fails before execution, the failed job may remain visible in the model list with status **Not started**. This state results from backend lifecycle handling, not customer configuration. | The backend automatically clears failed training jobs after approximately seven (7) days.<br><br>If earlier removal is required, submit an [Azure portal support request](https://ms.portal.azure.com/?quickstart=true#view/Microsoft_Azure_Support/HelpAndSupportBlade/~/overview). CSS or PG engineering can execute backend deletion of the orphaned training record. | April  2026 |
+| **2006** | Model accuracy | **Table recognition fails when a single page contains tables in different orientations** | The current pipeline generates a single unified rotation angle per image or page and applies it to all detected tables. Multiple table orientations within the same page aren't supported. Because layout is the first stage in the recognition pipeline, custom models don't mitigate this limitation. **Models affected:** All models (layout-stage limitation). | Preprocess the document before submission: detect the dominant orientation of each table region (for example, by inspecting PDF content-stream rotation values or applying image-analysis rotation detection), split the page into separate images—one per distinct orientation—and submit each as an independent Analyze request. Merge the structured results in your application layer. | June 2026 |
+| **2005** | Model accuracy | **Table extraction missing rows for single-row tables** | Single-row constructs aren't classified as tables in the current design. Rows may be missing from extraction output when the source document defines a table as a single row. This behavior is by design and may be refined in future releases. **Models affected:** All models.| Single-row table content is surfaced in the `paragraphs` or `keyValuePairs` arrays of the Analyze response rather than the `tables` array. Consume those arrays and retrieve the content. Alternatively, use the `boundingRegions` polygon coordinates from the `words` or `lines` arrays to reconstruct the row structure programmatically in post-processing. | June 2026 |
+| **2004** | Model accuracy | **OCR character ambiguity: 1 vs l and O vs 0** | Visually ambiguous character pairs (`1`/`l` and `O`/`0`) can be misclassified, particularly in serial-number-like fields that lack semantic context. The model applies linguistic context to improve accuracy for natural-language strings (for example, correcting `6OO` to `600` or `App1e` to `Apple`), but this heuristic isn't effective for alphanumeric identifiers. **Models affected:** All models. | Apply field-specific post-processing validation on the extracted `content` value. For serial-number or identifier fields, use a regular expression or character-allowlist check against the expected character set and apply substitution rules where `1`/`l` or `O`/`0` confusion is domain-predictable. Additionally, inspect per-word `confidence` scores in the `words` array to identify low-confidence spans and prioritize for targeted human review or automated correction. | June 2026 |
+| **2003** | Model accuracy | **OCR unable to detect superscript formatting** | Superscript-formatted characters aren't recognized as superscript. They're extracted as normal inline text without positional or formatting differentiation. **Models affected:** All models. | No model-level workaround is available; superscript detection is an OCR-stage limitation that custom model training doesn't address. As a post-processing alternative, compare the `polygon` or `boundingBox` coordinates of adjacent `word` spans within a `line` object in the Analyze response. Words whose vertical baseline is significantly elevated relative to surrounding words in the same line can be identified as likely superscripts and flagged or annotated accordingly in your application. | June 2026 |
+| **2002** | Model accuracy | **Dash (-) character misrecognized or returned as "1"** | An intermittent model quality issue causes the dash (`-`) character to be misrecognized or returned as the digit `1`. **Models affected:** All models. | No model-level workaround is available; this issue is an OCR-stage misrecognition that custom model training doesn't resolve. Apply post-processing validation on fields where a dash is a valid or expected value: use a regular expression or positional heuristic to identify isolated `1` characters that appear in separator or null-value positions (for example, between alphanumeric tokens or in fixed-width structured fields), and substitute them with a dash. Use per-word `confidence` scores to prioritize which extractions require correction. | June 2026 |
+| **2001** | Model accuracy | **Nested table structure not supported** | Document Intelligence prebuilt layout models don't support nested tables. Only the outermost table structure is extracted; inner nested tables aren't recognized as discrete table objects. **Models affected:** All models. | Custom extraction models and Content Understanding analyzers use the layout model as their first processing stage, so custom training doesn't resolve nested table detection. As a post-processing alternative, use the `boundingRegion` polygon coordinates returned for each detected `table` and `cell` object in the Analyze response to identify cell regions that spatially contain another detected table's bounding polygon. Use this overlap to reconstruct the parent-child nesting relationship programmatically in your application. | June 2026 |
+| **1005** | Model training | **Model training stuck in *Not started* status** | If a model training job fails before execution, the failed job may remain visible in the model list with status **Not started**. This state results from backend lifecycle handling, not customer configuration. | The backend automatically clears failed training jobs after approximately seven (7) days.<br><br>If earlier removal is required, submit an [Azure portal support request](https://ms.portal.azure.com/?quickstart=true#view/Microsoft_Azure_Support/HelpAndSupportBlade/~/overview). CSS or PG engineering can execute backend deletion of the orphaned training record. | April 2026 |
+| **1004** | Model training | **HTTP 500 – InternalServerError during model training (Neural or Template, Preview/GA APIs)** | Model training can fail with **HTTP 500 / InternalServerError**. This failure typically occurs when managed identity isn't configured correctly on the resource, especially in newer training flows. | Enable **Managed Identity** on your Document Intelligence resource.<br><br>Verify that the identity has the required permissions.<br><br>Follow the official [managed-identity configuration guidance](../authentication/managed-identities.md). | April 2026 |
+| **1003** | Model management | **Model Exists error when copying a model** | Copying a custom model can fail with a **Model Exists** error. This error occurs when a broken or partially created model remains on the target resource. Customers can't resolve this condition themselves. | No customer-side workaround is available.<br><br>Submit a [support request](mailto:formrecog_contact@microsoft.com) so the product group can remove the broken model from the backend. | April 2026 |
+| **1002** | Encryption | **ServiceUnavailable error when using CMK** | Operations that rely on **Customer‑Managed Keys (CMK)** can intermittently fail with a **service unavailable** error. This failure occurs when the storage service uses stale cached identity or key material. | **Option A:** Refresh the `CMK` cache. Disable and re-enable `CMK`, assign a new key, or associate a new managed identity.<br><br>**Option B:** Switch to **Microsoft-Managed Keys (MMK)**: Navigate to your Document Intelligence resource in the [Azure portal](https://portal.azure.com/). **Resource Management** → **Encryption** → **Microsoft Managed Keys**. | April 2026 |
+| **1001** | File types | **Content isn't supported error with Excel files** | Excel files are documented as a supported input type. Requests can fail with **Content isn't supported** when file content exceeds an internal character limit. This condition usually occurs with large or densely populated spreadsheets. | **Excel files larger than *~8,000,000 characters* are rejected**.<br><br>**Option A:** Split large Excel files into smaller files and submit them separately.<br><br>**Option B:** Switch to Azure [Content Understanding](../../content-understanding/overview.md), which uses improved parser logic for these files. | April 2026 |
 
 ## Related content
 
````
</details>

## articles/ai-services/language-service/conversational-language-understanding/overview.md{#item-bdc923}

<details>
<summary>Diff</summary>
````diff
@@ -14,7 +14,7 @@ ms.custom: language-service-clu
 # What is conversational language understanding?
 
 > [!IMPORTANT]
-> Conversational Language Understanding (CLU) is retiring from Azure Language effective **March 31, 2029**. After this date, the CLU feature is no longer supported.   During the support window, we recommend that users migrate existing workloads and direct all new projects to [Microsoft Foundry models](../../../foundry/concepts/foundry-models-overview.md), which offer enhanced capabilities for natural language understanding and can be easily integrated into your applications.
+> Conversational Language Understanding (CLU) retires from Azure Language on **March 31, 2029**. To avoid production disruption, migrate existing workloads and direct all new projects to [Microsoft Foundry](../../../foundry/concepts/foundry-models-overview.md), which offers enhanced capabilities for natural language understanding and can be easily integrated into your applications. For guidance, see [**Transitioning from Azure Language features to Foundry models**](https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/azure-ai-foundry-blog/transitioning-from-azure-language-features-to-foundry-models/4524092).
 
 Conversational language understanding is one of the custom features offered by [Azure Language](../overview.md). It's a cloud-based API service that applies machine-learning intelligence to enable you to build natural language understanding component to be used in an end-to-end conversational application.
 
````

 # What is custom text classification?
 
 > [!IMPORTANT]
-> Custom text classification is retiring from Azure Language effective **March 31, 2029**. After this date, the feature is no longer supported. During the support window, we recommend that users migrate existing workloads and direct all new projects to [Microsoft Foundry models](../../../foundry/concepts/foundry-models-overview.md), which offer enhanced capabilities for natural language understanding and can be easily integrated into your applications.
+> Custom text classification retires from Azure Language on **March 31, 2029**. To avoid production disruption, migrate existing workloads and direct all new projects to [Microsoft Foundry](../../../foundry/concepts/foundry-models-overview.md), which offers enhanced capabilities for natural language understanding and can be easily integrated into your applications. For guidance, see [**Transitioning from Azure Language features to Foundry models**](https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/azure-ai-foundry-blog/transitioning-from-azure-language-features-to-foundry-models/4524092).
 
 Custom text classification is one of the custom features offered by [Azure Language in Foundry Tools](../overview.md). It's a cloud-based API service that applies machine-learning intelligence to enable you to build custom models for text classification tasks.
 
````

+                "url": "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Gates",
+                "dataSource": "Wikipedia"
+            }, {
+                "bingId": "df2c4376-9923-6a54-893f-2ee5a5badbc7",
+                "name": "Paul Allen",
+                "matches": [{
+                    "text": "Paul Allen",
+                    "offset": 40,
+                    "length": 10,
+                    "confidenceScore": 0.54
+                }],
+                "language": "en",
+                "id": "Paul Allen",
+                "url": "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Allen",
+                "dataSource": "Wikipedia"
+            }, {
+                "bingId": "52535f87-235e-b513-54fe-c03e4233ac6e",
+                "name": "April 4",
+                "matches": [{
+                    "text": "April 4",
+                    "offset": 54,
+                    "length": 7,
+                    "confidenceScore": 0.38
+                }],
+                "language": "en",
+                "id": "April 4",
+                "url": "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/April_4",
+                "dataSource": "Wikipedia"
+            }],
+            "warnings": []
+        }],
+        "errors": [],
+        "modelVersion": "2021-06-01"
+    }
 }
 ```
 
````
</details>

## articles/ai-services/language-service/entity-linking/overview.md{#item-10e41c}

<details>
<summary>Diff</summary>
````diff
@@ -15,7 +15,7 @@ ms.custom: language-service-entity-linking
 # What is entity linking in Azure Language in Foundry Tools?
 
 > [!IMPORTANT]
-> Entity Linking is retiring from Azure Language in Foundry Tools effective **September 1, 2028**. After this date, the Entity Linking feature is no longer supported. During the support window, we recommend that users migrate existing workloads and direct all new projects to Azure Language [**Named Entity Recognition**](../named-entity-recognition/overview.md) or [Foundry models](../../../foundry/concepts/foundry-models-overview.md), which offer enhanced capabilities for natural language understanding and can be easily integrated into your applications.
+> Entity Linking retires from Azure Language on **September 1, 2028**. To avoid production disruption, migrate existing workloads and direct all new projects to Azure Language [**Named Entity Recognition**](../named-entity-recognition/overview.md) or [Microsoft Foundry](../../../foundry/concepts/foundry-models-overview.md). These options provide enhanced natural language understanding capabilities and integrate directly into your applications. For guidance, see [**Transitioning from Azure Language features to Foundry models**](https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/azure-ai-foundry-blog/transitioning-from-azure-language-features-to-foundry-models/4524092).
 
 Entity linking is one of the features offered by [Language](../overview.md), a collection of machine learning and AI algorithms in the cloud for developing intelligent applications that involve written language. Entity linking identifies and disambiguates the identity of entities found in text. For example, in the sentence "*We went to Seattle last week.*", the word "*Seattle*" would be identified, with a link to more information on Wikipedia.
 
````
</details>

## articles/ai-services/language-service/key-phrase-extraction/overview.md{#item-4ff047}

<details>
<summary>Diff</summary>
````diff
@@ -14,7 +14,7 @@ ms.custom: language-service-key-phrase
 # What is key phrase extraction in Azure Language in Foundry Tools?
 
 > [!IMPORTANT]
-> Key phrase extraction is retiring from Azure Language effective **March 31, 2029**. After this date, the feature is no longer supported. During the support window, we recommend that users migrate existing workloads and direct all new projects to [Microsoft Foundry models](../../../foundry/concepts/foundry-models-overview.md), which offer enhanced capabilities for natural language understanding and can be easily integrated into your applications.
+> Key phrase extraction retires from Azure Language on **March 31, 2029**. To avoid production disruption, migrate existing workloads and direct all new projects to [Microsoft Foundry](../../../foundry/concepts/foundry-models-overview.md), which offers enhanced capabilities for natural language understanding and can be easily integrated into your applications. For guidance, see [**Transitioning from Azure Language features to Foundry models**](https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/azure-ai-foundry-blog/transitioning-from-azure-language-features-to-foundry-models/4524092).
 
 Key phrase extraction is one of the features offered by [Azure Language in Foundry Tools](../overview.md). This capability is part of a suite of cloud-based machine learning and AI tools designed for building intelligent applications that process written language. Use key phrase extraction to quickly identify the main concepts in text. For example, in the text "*The food was delicious and the staff were wonderful.*", key phrase extraction returns the main topics: "*food*" and "*wonderful staff*."
 
````
</details>

この更新は、特に画像やメディアファイルが多く使われる技術文書においては、継続的な管理が必要であることを示しており、ユーザーに最新の視覚的リソースを提供することの重要性を強調しています。

## articles/ai-services/language-service/orchestration-workflow/overview.md{#item-53d49f}

<details>
<summary>Diff</summary>
````diff
@@ -14,7 +14,7 @@ ms.custom: language-service-orchestration
 # What is orchestration workflow?
 
 > [!IMPORTANT]
-> Orchestration workflow is retiring from Azure Language effective **March 31, 2029**. After this date, the orchestration workflow feature is no longer supported. During the support window, we recommend that users migrate existing workloads and direct all new projects to [Microsoft Foundry models](../../../foundry/concepts/foundry-models-overview.md), which offer enhanced capabilities for natural language understanding and can be easily integrated into your applications.
+> Orchestration workflow retires from Azure Language on **March 31, 2029**. To avoid production disruption, migrate existing workloads and direct all new projects to [Microsoft Foundry](../../../foundry/concepts/foundry-models-overview.md), which offers enhanced capabilities for natural language understanding and can be easily integrated into your applications. For guidance, see [**Transitioning from Azure Language features to Foundry models**](https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/azure-ai-foundry-blog/transitioning-from-azure-language-features-to-foundry-models/4524092).
 
 Orchestration workflow is one of the features offered by [Azure Language in Foundry Tools](../overview.md). This cloud-based API service uses machine learning to facilitate the development of orchestration models that seamlessly integrate [Conversational Language Understanding (CLU)](../conversational-language-understanding/overview.md) and [Custom question Answering](../question-answering/overview.md) projects.
 Developers can create an orchestration workflow to iteratively tag utterances, train models, and evaluate their performance before deployment.
````
</details>

    "modification_type": "minor update",

### Explanation
この変更は、「overview.md」ファイルに関連しており、オーケストレーションワークフロー機能の引退に関する告知文の言い回しを改良するためのマイナーな修正です。具体的には、「オーケストレーションワークフローが2029年3月31日以降にサポートされなくなる」という重要なメッセージが、より明確で利用者に配慮した形に書き換えられています。

新しい文言では、「生産環境の混乱を避けるために、既存のワークロードを移行し、すべての新しいプロジェクトをMicrosoft Foundryに向けてください」と記載され、ユーザーに対する具体的な対応策が示されています。また、「Azure Languageの機能からFoundryモデルへの移行」といった追加のガイダンスを提供するリンクも含まれています。

この修正は、ユーザーがオーケストレーションワークフロー機能の終了に備えるためのより的確な情報を提供し、適切な移行手続きを促進することを目的としています。オーケストレーションワークフローは、Azure Languageの重要な機能の一つであり、機械学習を活用してアプリケーションにおける自然言語理解を支援するために設計されています。したがって、利用者がこの変更に迅速に対応できるようにすることは、サービスの継続性とユーザーエクスペリエンスの向上に寄与します。

変更がない場合でも、背景や使用コンテキストに関連するメタデータの調整などが行われていることがあります。このような更新は、全体のドキュメントが合理的で最新の情報を提供できるようにするために重要です。ユーザーは、適切な情報を得ることで、AIエージェント作成のプロセスにおいて、よりスムーズな体験を得ることができます。

 Sentiment analysis and opinion mining are features offered by [Azure Language](../overview.md), a collection of machine learning and AI algorithms in the cloud for developing intelligent applications that involve written language. These features help you discover what people think about your brand or topic by analyzing text for signs of positive or negative sentiment.
